=== EXAMPLE 0 ===
English: My grandfather, a man by the name of White Mexican Clansman, and another man called The Son of Former Sweathouse, were the only men. They and several womenfolk worked hard on me.
Navajo: Shichei ńt’éé’ Naakai Dine’é Łigaii wolyéé ńt’éé’ dóó ła’ dó’ Diné Táchéhéni’ Biye’ wolyéé ńt’éé’ ’éí shį́į́ t’éiyá diné nilį́įgo dóó sáanii dó’ díkwíí shį́į́ kwii shaa naanish bííghą́ą́’


English: They were to go by way of Lukachukai, Tsaile, and Crystal, and on over to Fort Defiance.
Navajo: Nagháí Lók’a’jíkai góne’ dóó Tsééhílį́į́ góne’ dóó Sǫ’ Siláágóó dóó ńléí Tséhootsooíjį’


English: Wait.
Navajo: T’aháloo


English: The two of them built the trading post at the place called Blue Clay Point.
Navajo: ’Áko ’éí yaa ndilt’éego Bis Dootł’izh Deez’áhí hoolyéegi naalyéhé bá hooghan ’áhoolaa


English: Soldiers came from Fort Defiance.
Navajo: Tséhootsooídę́ę́’ siláago níná


English: My forbears, the old men and women folk, were of the Mexican People Clan. With great hardship they came back from the place called Fort Sumner, packing their goods on their backs, and afterward lived here at Lukachukai.
Navajo:

Navajo: ’Éí shį́į́ haayáá lá jiní

Navajo: Aadóó ’ákǫ́ǫ́ dashdiiyá


English: Then we started to follow the sheep again.
Navajo: ’Aadóó dibé bikéé’ dah náádiit’áázh


English: So we went in.
Navajo: T’áá ’áko wóne’é yah ’iit’áázh jiní


English: Here they began life anew.

=== EXAMPLE 2 ===
English: Then we followed the ridge up over Black Mountain.
Navajo: ’Aadóó ’eii Dziłíjiin dah sitą́ t’áá bikáá’góó náániikai


English: And some moved over to Black Mountain.
Navajo: Ła’ Dziłíjiin bída’iyiinééh


English: When they moved over to the mountains they went in wagons.
Navajo: Ńléí dził bída’iyiináago ’ákǫ́ǫ́ tsinaabąąs da bee da’níná


English: The two of them built the trading post at the place called Blue Clay Point.
Navajo: ’Áko ’éí yaa ndilt’éego Bis Dootł’izh Deez’áhí hoolyéegi naalyéhé bá hooghan ’áhoolaa


English: So they moved up onto the mountain.
Navajo: ’Áko diné lą’í dził yighą́ą́’ hadahineesdzood


English: Then from their home at a place called Spring in the Clay they started moving over and across yonder mountain.
Navajo: 

================================================================================

=== EXAMPLE 3 ===
English: As they were taking him outside I crawled and squeezed myself out among them.
Navajo: Kǫ́ǫ́ yił yijahgo t’áá ’atát’ah ch’ínísh’na’


English: Then he went back to where the noise came from, and found a baby lying there, it is said.
Navajo: ’Aadóó nát’ą́ą́ ’áajį’ dah nízhdiidzáá ńt’éé’ kǫ́ǫ́ ’awéé’ léi’ sitį́ jiní


English: It is said that, in the past, the people really made it a point to teach one another.
Navajo: T’ah nahdę́ę́’ diné t’áá yéego nda’ahinitin ńt’éé’ daaní


English: It was said that they would never return.
Navajo: Doo nízhdookah da


English: It was said that the first word of this had come from up north.
Navajo: Nagháí náhookǫsdę́ę’go ’áłtsé hane’ yit’ą́ hodoo’niid


English: While they were making this move they stopped for the night, and it is said that I was born where they halted.

=== EXAMPLE 6 ===
English: And it turned out that my grandfather, who was called Big Mexican Clansman, was there too.
Navajo: Shichei Naakaii Dine’étsoh wolyéé ńt’éé’ ’éí dó’ sidáá lá


English: I had an uncle by the name of Forked House. He was a young man, and he adopted me.
Navajo: Shidá’í ńt’éé’ T’iisyaa Bikiní wolyéé ńt’éé’ tsíłkę́ę́h nilį́įgo ’éí ’áyaa nikishidiilt’e’


English: So then my grandfather, the man I spoke of as Big Mexican Clansman, volunteered to join him
Navajo: ’Áko shį́į́ shichei yę́ę Naakaii Dine’étsoh wolyé dishnínę́ę bił ’ahizhdii’áázh


English: And a man by the name of Black Horse caused the trouble.
Navajo: ’Áádóó diné ła’ Bilį́į́’ Łizhinii wolyéé ńt’éé’ ’éí dó’ naazhchxǫ’


English: A man by the name of Black Horse was the leader of that faction.
Navajo: Bilį́į́’ Łizhinii joolyéé ńt’éé’ ’éí ’áájí ’ákót’éego bee dah ’ajoo’ish ńt’éé


English: My grandfather, a man by the name of White Mexican Clansman, and another man called The Son of Former Sweathouse, were the only men. They and several womenfolk worked hard on me.
Navajo:

=== EXAMPLE 7 ===
English: Once we had billy goats in the herd.
Navajo: Tł’ízí chǫǫh dó’ ’atahgo bił na’niilkaad ńt’éé’ łah


English: My cousin followed me.
Navajo: Shił naa’aash dó’ t’áá shikéé’ joolwoł


English: He had a wagon and a team.
Navajo: Bitsinaabąąs hólǫ́ǫgo bilį́į́’ na’ałbąąsii hólǫ́ǫgo


English: We had one billy goat in the herd that was just a little bit mean.
Navajo: Tł’ízí ką’ ła’ t’áá bíyó hashkéego bił na’niilkaad ńt’éé’


English: We had a large herd of sheep.
Navajo: Dibé lą’í da naniilkaad


English: My grandfather had a fine wether goat that he was quite proud of. He killed it there, and the people feasted with great joy.

=== EXAMPLE 8 ===
English: Like on that other occasion, there was again a lot of fog.
Navajo: T’áá ńléí ’áłtséédą́ą́’ ’át’éhę́ęgi ’át’éego ’áhí bee náánátł’éé’ lá


English: They started moving.
Navajo: Yinéél baa ńda’diildee’


English: Then we started to follow the sheep again.
Navajo: ’Aadóó dibé bikéé’ dah náádiit’áázh


English: On the day following the night on which she gave birth to me, my mother went on foot as far as the people moved that day.
Navajo: Shimá tł’éédą́ą́’ shijishchį́įgo t’áá ni’ jiníyá jiní níwohjį’ haa shį́į́ nízahgi ni’ínéehgo ’áajį’


English: On the next day, February 4, we took off again.
Navajo: Biiskání dį́’ígóó yoołkáałgo nihił dah nááda’diit’a’


English: Then on the day following the night of my birth we again started to move.
Navajo:

=== EXAMPLE 14 ===
English: The custom of building a separate home in connection with those who marry will go on into the future.
Navajo: ’Índa díí k’ad ni’ąą nahalindi ’ayéhé bá hooghan ’ályaaígíí ’éí kodóó náás yidiiską́ą́góó ’índa hool’áágóó t’áá ’ákót’éego bik’ehgóó ’áhoot’ée dooleeł


English: Wait.
Navajo: T’aháloo


English: In one case they were taking a woman to jail and she fell unconscious.
Navajo: ’Éí ’éí siláago ła’ sáanii t’áá tádazhdiyeehgo doo bił ’ééhoozin da lá ’akon


English: But today we are lax and do not teach our children much.
Navajo: Yéego na’anitin yee ’ałch’į’ yádaalti’go kót’éego ła’ tsíłkéí yá’át’éhgo biyaa dahoo’a’


English: As a result, when people got sick they really suffered everywhere.
Navajo: Jó ’ákót’éego diné bąąh dah dahoo’a’go diné t’áá ’íiyisíí ti’dahooznii’ ni’ daałahgóó


English: Nowadays when a woman gives birth they take special care of her, telling her not to catch cold.
Navajo:

Navajo: Ła’ shį́į́ daaháí ní hóla


English: As time goes on, a child develops his thinking from his mother and father.

English: I do not remember in detail much of what happened before I was about ten years old.
Navajo: Neeznáá daats’í shinááhai dóó ’índa t’áá kóníghání nahalingo ’énáshniihgo hodideeshzhiizh


English: As time went on I somehow grew up. I do not remember much about it.

=== EXAMPLE 18 ===
English: My cousin followed me.
Navajo: Shił naa’aash dó’ t’áá shikéé’ joolwoł


English: My cousin would tell me to go a certain direction, and we would then separate.
Navajo: ’Áádóó ’ałts’á shiit’áázh łahjí ’aninááh shijinígo


English: Then in the morning when we would take out the sheep he would again remind me of this lesson.
Navajo: ’Áko ’abínígo dah náádí’níilkaadgo ninááshizhneestą́ą́’


English: When dawn came First Man got up.
Navajo: ’Ałtsé Hastiin wolyéii hayííłką́ago ch’ínáádzídzá


English: But morning came and nothing had happened.
Navajo: Ńt’éé’ ’éí t’áadoo ’áhóót’įįdígóó yiską́


English: When morning would come and I would be sleeping nicely, my grandfather would throw me out of bed.
Navajo:

=== EXAMPLE 23 ===
English: because he protected me.
Navajo: Shich’ą́ą́h ’ííyá nisingo


English: My cousin followed me.
Navajo: Shił naa’aash dó’ t’áá shikéé’ joolwoł


English: That is the way my grandfather drove me about and spoke to me.
Navajo: Shichei yę́ę ’ákót’éego t’áá nashineeyood dóó t’áá shich’į’ yááłti’


English: You cannot escape them anyway," my uncle and my grandfather said to us.
Navajo: Háadish dó’ baa dáádidooh’ash nihizhdííniid shidá’í yę́ę dóó shichei yę́ę


English: You will gain nothing by it," my grandfather said to me. He told me this story and gave me instructions on top of it.
Navajo: Dóó ts’ídá t’áadoo bee ńdidííléłí da shiłníigo shicheii ńt’éé shił nahasne’ dóó t’áá yiláahjį’ shich’į’ yááłti’


English: If you are strong you will lie hudled in death only after the dirt is torn and furrowed around you (i.e. you will give up only after a struggle)," my grandfather used to tell me.
Navajo:

=== EXAMPLE 27 ===

Navajo: ’Áko ’ákwe’é bee bił hwiilne’


English: and they no doubt came with evil thoughts. The people who, lived hereabout had heard nothing of their plans

Navajo: Tó hódeeskai daha’níigo dahane’ t’áá hazhó’ó diné lą’í da’oodlą́ągo dził yídahiináa ni’


English: God punished us.
Navajo: God wolyéii ’atínihiilaa


English: This is what happened.
Navajo: ’Ákódzaa jiní


English: There is a passage where God says that the people will be punished, and that's what happened.
Navajo:
